<p><i><b>Talk That Talk</b></i> is the sixth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbadian_people" title="Barbadian people">Barbadian</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, released on November 18, 2011, by <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a> and SRP Records. It was recorded while traveling for the <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a> between February and November 2011, and was originally planned to be a <a href="/wiki/Reissue" title="Reissue">reissue</a> of her previous studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Loud_(Rihanna_album)" title="Loud (Rihanna album)">Loud</a></i> (2010). As executive producer, Rihanna enlisted a wide range of producers including <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangladesh_(producer)" title="Bangladesh (producer)">Mr. Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chase_%26_Status" title="Chase &amp; Status">Chase &amp; Status</a>, Cirkut, Da Internz, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Luke" title="Dr. Luke">Dr. Luke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ester_Dean" title="Ester Dean">Ester Dean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pendulum_(drum_and_bass_band)" title="Pendulum (drum and bass band)">Gareth McGrillen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/No_I.D." title="No I.D.">No I.D.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Priscilla_Renea" title="Priscilla Renea">Priscilla Renea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rob_Swire" title="Rob Swire">Rob Swire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" title="Stargate (production team)">StarGate</a>, <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>. Following in the same vein as <i>Loud</i>, <i>Talk That Talk</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">dance</a>-oriented <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>/<a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub.com_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-avclub.com-3">[3]</a></sup> crossover album that incorporates elements of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house</a> music. The album also continues to have subtle <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> genres, whilst its lyrical content and themes revolve around a nihilist, romantic and lascivious lover.</p>
<p><i>Talk That Talk</i> received generally positive reviews from music critics, and debuted at number three on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with first-week sales of 198,000 copies. As of June 2015, the album has sold 1.15 million copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-4">[4]</a></sup> The album peaked at number one in Austria, New Zealand, Norway, Switzerland and the United Kingdom, where it debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, selling 163,000 copies in its first week. As of April 2012, the album has been certified triple Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI) for shipments of 900,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPI_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> "<a href="/wiki/We_Found_Love" title="We Found Love">We Found Love</a>" became Rihanna's eleventh number-one song US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, and topped the charts in 26 additional countries. "<a href="/wiki/You_da_One" title="You da One">You da One</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Talk_That_Talk_(Rihanna_song)" title="Talk That Talk (Rihanna song)">Talk That Talk</a>" (featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>) and a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Birthday_Cake_(song)#Remix_featuring_Chris_Brown" title="Birthday Cake (song)">Birthday Cake</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a>) experienced moderate success, while "<a href="/wiki/Where_Have_You_Been" title="Where Have You Been">Where Have You Been</a>" reached the top ten of twenty countries around the world. A remixed form of "<a href="/wiki/Cockiness_(Love_It)#Remix_featuring_ASAP_Rocky" title="Cockiness (Love It)">Cockiness (Love It)</a>" (featuring rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A$AP_Rocky" title="A$AP Rocky">A$AP Rocky</a>) was released as the sixth and final single from the record.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna,_LOUD_Tour,_Florida_6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_6.jpg/220px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_6.jpg/330px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_6.jpg/440px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna,_LOUD_Tour,_Florida_6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Recording for the album began during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Loud_Tour" title="The Loud Tour">The Loud Tour</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the release of Rihanna's previous studio album, <i>Loud</i> (2010), the singer revealed via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> that the album would be re-issued with new songs and released in fall 2011, writing that "[the] [<i>Loud</i> era] continues with more new music to add to [your] collection".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BET_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-BET-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fall2011_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fall2011-7">[7]</a></sup> In September 2011, Rihanna took to Twitter to confirm that plans for a re-issue of <i>Loud</i> had been scrapped, with the singer tweeting "I [thought about] a [re-release], but LOUD is its own body of work! Plus [you] guys work so [fucking] hard that [you] deserve to act brand new."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In an interview with <i>Mixtape Daily</i>, producer Verse Simmonds, half of the duo The Jugganauts, who wrote and produced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reggae_music" title="Reggae music">reggae</a>-infused song "<a href="/wiki/Man_Down_(song)" title="Man Down (song)">Man Down</a>" from <i>Loud</i>, revealed that the singer was nearing completion of her sixth studio album in August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juggernauts_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Juggernauts-9">[9]</a></sup> The duo also said that they had penned two tracks for possible inclusion on the album, saying "From what I understand, she is closing the album up now, and we did two records for her that she really, really loved and I'm really excited about them as well" and also expressed interest in writing a third song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juggernauts_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Juggernauts-9">[9]</a></sup> On September 15, 2011, Rihanna confirmed via her official Twitter account that recording sessions for the album were indeed underway, tweeting "I can't wait to start filling u guys in on some details!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TweetsAboutNewAlbum_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-TweetsAboutNewAlbum-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rihanna created a <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> campaign page entitled "Rihanna: UNLOCKED" [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>], whereby her fans on Facebook are given missions to complete, in the form of games, in order to "unlock" new information about the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMEUnlocked_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-NMEUnlocked-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DigitalSpyUnlocked_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-DigitalSpyUnlocked-12">[12]</a></sup> Upon the unveiling of the standard edition's artwork, both James Dinh of <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> and a reviewer for <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> commented that Rihanna looks "seductive" in the image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Artwork_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Artwork-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Gordon Smart of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> humorously criticized the standard edition artwork by saying that it looks as though the singer is trying to cover up a cold sore with her tongue, writing "It's easy to pick them up at this time of year – especially as she's constantly naked or attached to her new boyfriend Dudley O'Shaughnessy by the lips."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheSunArtowkr_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheSunArtowkr-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Recording sessions for <i>Talk That Talk</i> began in February 2011 and ended in November 2011. The album was recorded in various recording studios. Singer-songwriters and producers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean Combs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ester_Dean" title="Ester Dean">Ester Dean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Luke" title="Dr. Luke">Dr. Luke</a> and <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a> contributed to the album. Kuk Harrell, one of the producers of Talk That Talk, spoke on the recording of the album saying: "In addition to touring, we are recording Rihanna's new album. We have a portable studio that we set up at the different hotels that we are staying at. We set up shop anywhere in the hotel. Before we went on the European leg of Rihanna's Loud tour, we started recording the album in Los Angeles. Rihanna likes to work late hours, so she would come into the studio at 9pm and work until 6am."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In May 2012, Rihanna revealed that whilst she was recording the album, she suffered from exhaustion, saying in part: "It was the best [shit] ever, it was some rock star [shit] This is the craziest schedule I've ever been on in my entire life. One morning I woke up and started crying so hard. I finally just got to my bed from the IV [drip] and I was just like, 'Good I can actually get to sleep tonight', because we stayed up all night' and I finished [the album] at 5 pm the day before..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_lyrics">Music and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Music and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Talk That Talk</i> is a danceable <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>/<a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> crossover<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub.com_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-avclub.com-3">[3]</a></sup> album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosen_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen-1">[1]</a></sup> comprising uptempo <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">club</a> tracks, raunchy pop songs, and mid-tempo inspirational ballads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PitchforkReview_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-PitchforkReview-18">[18]</a></sup> It also incorporates elements of <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, and <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-19">[19]</a></sup> Most of the songs feature heavy bass and coarse sounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-19">[19]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Electro_(music)" title="Electro (music)">electro</a> beats and imposing <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lachno_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lachno-20">[20]</a></sup> James Lachno of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> cites <i>Talk That Talk</i> as Rihanna's "most club-ready album to date",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lachno_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lachno-20">[20]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> calls it "pop without shame—her <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hookiest</a> and most dance-targeted album, decorated with a thoughtful assortment of suitably titillating blats, noodles, dubs, groans, hiccups, boom-booms, cut-ups, speed-ups, <a href="/wiki/The_xx" title="The xx">xx</a> samples, and spoken-word bits."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christgau_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-21">[21]</a></sup> Jon Caramanica of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> writes that Rihanna's version of dance music on the album draws on "the club music of the early 1990s".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times-2">[2]</a></sup> The album's lyrics posit Rihanna as a nihilist romantic and lascivious lover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferrier_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrier-22">[22]</a></sup> The album also has subtle <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> influences,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lachno_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lachno-20">[20]</a></sup> with slower songs that have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double-time" title="Double-time">double</a>-<a href="/wiki/Snare_drum" title="Snare drum">snare</a> <a href="/wiki/Riddim" title="Riddim">riddims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-19">[19]</a></sup> Music journalist <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kot" title="Greg Kot">Greg Kot</a> observes that, along with droning <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a> sounds, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_music" title="Caribbean music">Caribbean</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_music" title="Eastern music">Eastern</a> touches from past Rihanna albums get recycled into bombastic dance tunes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kot_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kot-23">[23]</a></sup> Apart from its sexual innuendo, <i>Talk That Talk</i> features odes to dysfunctional love and universal love.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-19">[19]</a></sup> Christgau interprets the lyrics to be "associating carnality with love" and writes that the album "celebrates the relationship of sex to love rather than pain," before leaning on "heart songs and theme statements" in the second half."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christgau_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

</div>

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">A 17-second sample of "You da One<span style="padding-right:.2em;">"</span>'s chorus, which features the <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">mid-tempo</a> <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" title="Synthpop">electropop</a> composition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSComposition_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-DSComposition-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YDOBillboardReview_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-YDOBillboardReview-25">[25]</a></sup></div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The opening track, "You Da One", which was produced by <a href="/wiki/Dr._Luke" title="Dr. Luke">Dr. Luke</a>, is a bouncy mid-tempo song with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Caribbean_music_genres" title="List of Caribbean music genres">Caribbean</a> flavor, and features a <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a> influenced breakdown towards the middle of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstListen_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FirstListen-26">[26]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Where_Have_You_Been" title="Where Have You Been">Where Have You Been</a>", produced by Dr. Luke and <a href="/wiki/Ester_Dean" title="Ester Dean">Ester Dean</a>, runs through an acoustic beat and incorporates elements of <a href="/wiki/Trance_music" title="Trance music">trance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstListen_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-FirstListen-26">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/We_Found_Love" title="We Found Love">We Found Love</a>", is an <a href="/wiki/Electro_house" title="Electro house">electro house</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The title track features rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and samples <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>'s "I Got a Story to Tell".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstListen_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-FirstListen-26">[26]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Roc_Me_Out" title="Roc Me Out">Roc Me Out</a>" is set in "chugging" tempo and features heavy <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synths</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popdust_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-popdust-29">[29]</a></sup> The tenth track, "<a href="/wiki/Watch_n%27_Learn" title="Watch n' Learn">Watch n' Learn</a>", features a flirtatious and playful hip pop melody with grinding synths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstListen_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-FirstListen-26">[26]</a></sup> The final standard edition track of the album, "Farewell", is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballad_(music)" title="Ballad (music)">ballad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstListen_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-FirstListen-26">[26]</a></sup> The song was written by <a href="/wiki/Ester_Dean" title="Ester Dean">Ester Dean</a> and Alexander Grant, with production helmed by Grant under his production name <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_notes_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Album_notes-30">[30]</a></sup> "Farewell" contains lyrics that revolve around saying goodbye to a lover who is not able to be physically present in the relationship for long periods of time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T.27Cha_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-T.27Cha-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWAlbumReview_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-EWAlbumReview-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Instrumentation" title="Instrumentation">Instrumentation</a> consists of a rolling <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Additional tracks released on the deluxe edition of <i>Talk That Talk</i> include the songs "Red Lipstick", "Do Ya Thang", and "Fool in Love". "Red Lipstick" is described as a "dark 'n' twisted" dubstep number which was written by The Dream and Rihanna and produced by the two along with production duo <a href="/wiki/Chase_%26_Status" title="Chase &amp; Status">Chase &amp; Status</a>, who first worked with the singer on her fourth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a>, <i>Rated R</i> (2009). "Do Ya Thang" is a <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">contemporary R&amp;B</a> track with a subtle hook and a simple message. It was written and produced by Rihanna and The-Dream. "Fool in Love" is a <a href="/wiki/Rhapsody_(music)" title="Rhapsody (music)">rhapsodic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopCrush_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopCrush-34">[34]</a></sup> ballad which incorporates acoustic and electric guitars, synthesizers, and drums, and has received comparisons to <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Criminal_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Criminal (Britney Spears song)">Criminal</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FoolInLovePopdust_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FoolInLovePopdust-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p><i>Talk That Talk</i> received generally positive reviews from critics. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream publications, the album received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 64, based on 27 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>'s Andy Kellman dubbed it Rihanna's "third best album to date ... behind <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad_(Rihanna_album)" title="Good Girl Gone Bad (Rihanna album)">Good Girl Gone Bad</a></i> (2007) and <i><a href="/wiki/Rated_R_(Rihanna_album)" title="Rated R (Rihanna album)">Rated R</a></i> (2009)," and stated, "Minus the fluff, it's close to the latter's equal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-am_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-am-36">[36]</a></sup> Jon Caramanica of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> wrote that the album places Rihanna "squarely at the center of the pop genre best suited for a singer of her fundamental evanescence – dance music, which conveniently is the mode du jour of contemporary R&amp;B and pop."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times-2">[2]</a></sup> James Lachno of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> called it "an adrenalised behemoth of a record which reasserts her position as one of pop's most compulsive pleasures".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lachno_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lachno-20">[20]</a></sup> Rebecca Nicholson of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> called it "a blast of obnoxious, filth-fuelled pop" and felt that "it works best when the music hall bawdiness is left aside in favour of bleak euphoria".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholson_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholson-37">[37]</a></sup> In a review of its deluxe edition for <i><a href="/wiki/MSN_Music" title="MSN Music">MSN Music</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> complimented the songs' carnal lyrics and stated, "I prefer it to her earlier albums because I find its many porny moments titillating."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christgau_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a mixed review, Randall Roberts of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> expressed dissatisfaction with the themes of the album and stated, "The singer works that NC-17 territory, but the sauciness sometimes borders on shtick. With an eye toward Middle America, it's mostly just insinuation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-19">[19]</a></sup> Greg Kot of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> panned its "double or <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/single_entendre" title="wikt:single entendre">single entendres</a>", and felt that it gives the impression of "a chintzy <a href="/wiki/Softcore_pornography" title="Softcore pornography">soft-core porn</a> movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kot_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kot-23">[23]</a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> said that Rihanna mostly "struggles to assert her vocal character against a sea of effects".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gill_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gill-38">[38]</a></sup> Matthew Cole from <i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></i> panned it as "pretty easily the worst Rihanna album yet".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slant_review_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slant_review-43">[43]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Lindsay Zoladz wrote that the album "tries too hard to send a more one-dimensional message" than other pop artists in 2011, adding that it "ends up falling flat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PitchforkReview_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-PitchforkReview-18">[18]</a></sup> Priya Elan of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> found it "annoyingly safe" and wrote that it "leaves us with the impression Rihanna has spread herself so thinly that she doesn’t have time to record a cohesive album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elan_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elan-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album debuted at number three on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, with first-week sales of 198,000 copies in the United States, slightly below her last album, which also debuted at number three with 207,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In its second week, the album sold an additional 68,200 copies in the United States, dropping to number 7 on the charts and bringing its total sales to 266,400 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The album has been certified Platinum in the United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> and has sold 1,150,000 copies as of June 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, the album was certified Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI) for shipments of 300,000 units after six days of sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPI_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-5">[5]</a></sup> <i>Talk That Talk</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, selling more than 163,000 copies in its first week. With the album and "<a href="/wiki/We_Found_Love" title="We Found Love">We Found Love</a>" both at number one, it made Rihanna the only female artist in the UK to simultaneously have a number one single and album twice in the same year with a different album and single. The other double chart topper being "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Name%3F_(Rihanna_song)" title="What's My Name? (Rihanna song)">What's My Name?</a>" and <i><a href="/wiki/Loud_(Rihanna_album)" title="Loud (Rihanna album)">Loud</a></i> in January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> On December 9, 2011 the album was certified two-times Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI) for shipments of 600,000 copies in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> As of June 26, 2012 it has sold 850,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> It was the second biggest selling R&amp;B / hip hop album of 2011 in the UK, only beaten by Rihanna's previous album, <i><a href="/wiki/Loud_(Rihanna_album)" title="Loud (Rihanna album)">Loud</a></i> (2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> On August 12, 2012, the album returned to the number one position of the UK Albums Chart, selling 9,578 copies, making it the UK's lowest-selling number one since records began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The record was beaten 4 years later by <a href="/wiki/Blossoms_(band)" title="Blossoms (band)">Blossoms</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Blossoms_(album)" title="Blossoms (album)">self-titled album</a></i> which sold 7,948 copies on August 19, 2016.</p>
<p>As of March 2013, the album has sold more than 5.5 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2160" data-file-width="3840" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg/270px-Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg/405px-Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg/540px-Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg 2x" width="270"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_-_We_Found_Love_-_Birmingham_Loud_Tour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rihanna performing "<a href="/wiki/We_Found_Love" title="We Found Love">We Found Love</a>" during her <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a> in November 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/We_Found_Love" title="We Found Love">We Found Love</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a>, was released as the lead single from the album, premiering on September 22, 2011 in the United Kingdom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeadSingle_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-LeadSingle-53">[53]</a></sup> and being released the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AU_release_TTT_single_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-AU_release_TTT_single-54">[54]</a></sup> Critical reaction was mixed. They criticized the lack of lyrical content, with many citing the lyrics as second best to the song's production and composition, though they praised Harris's production of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Priya_Elan_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Priya_Elan-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamboa1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamboa1-56">[56]</a></sup> The music video, which premiered on October 19, 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RapUpVidPremiere_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-RapUpVidPremiere-57">[57]</a></sup> depicts the singer as a drug abusing thrill seeker in a relationship that quickly spirals downward into addiction and violence. "We Found Love" debuted at number 16 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, eventually reaching number one, giving Rihanna the record for a solo artist to have amassed twenty top ten singles in the shortest amount of time in the history of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USChartDebut_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-USChartDebut-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FourthWeek_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FourthWeek-59">[59]</a></sup> The song also peaked at number one in Denmark, France, Ireland, Norway, Sweden, Germany and the United Kingdom, for six weeks.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/You_da_One" title="You da One">You da One</a>" was released as the second single from the album, having its radio premiere on November 11 and being released digitally on November 14, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ArgentinaiTunes_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ArgentinaiTunes-60">[60]</a></sup> "You da One" was sent to US mainstream radio on November 29, 2011. The single was a moderate success, reaching the top twenty of the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> peaking at fourteen as well as reaching the top twenty of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> peaking at sixteen, while also topping the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> chart, and attaining top twenty positions in eleven other countries.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Talk_That_Talk_(Rihanna_song)" title="Talk That Talk (Rihanna song)">Talk That Talk</a>", was confirmed as the third single from the album by Rihanna on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, following a vote from her fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The song, which features a rap verse from Jay-Z, was serviced to urban radio in the United States on January 17, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radio_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-radio-62">[62]</a></sup> It reached number 31 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and 25 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Birthday_Cake_(song)#Remix_featuring_Chris_Brown" title="Birthday Cake (song)">Birthday Cake</a>" was released as a full length remix version featuring former boyfriend <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_entertainer)" title="Chris Brown (American entertainer)">Chris Brown</a> on February 20, 2012, coinciding with Rihanna's 24th birthday. It was sent to radio as the fourth single from the album on March 6, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UrbanRadio_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-UrbanRadio-63">[63]</a></sup> The official remix reached number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a>, subsequently managing a peak of number 24 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, despite no digital release of the remix or music video.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Where_Have_You_Been" title="Where Have You Been">Where Have You Been</a>" was released as the fifth single from the album, impacting Top 40/Mainstream radio in the US on May 8, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Following the release of the music video, it reached number five on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart and within the top ten of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> at number six.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> When "Where Have You Been" peaked inside of the top ten of the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, Rihanna became the artist who had gained the most top ten entries in the shortest time span, with 22 top ten singles in 7 years, displacing <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Cockiness_(Love_It)" title="Cockiness (Love It)">Cockiness (Love It)</a>" was released as the sixth and final single on September 7, 2012 in a remixed form of the original version and features rapper <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Rocky" title="ASAP Rocky">ASAP Rocky</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Upon the release of <i>Talk That Talk</i>, the song debuted on multiple world charts. The song debuted on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaon_Chart" title="Gaon Chart">South Korea Gaon International Chart</a> at number 62 on November 26, 2011, with sales of 6,918 digital downloads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SouthKoreaDebut_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-SouthKoreaDebut-66">[66]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, "Cockiness (Love It)" debuted at number 33 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_R%26B_Chart" title="UK R&amp;B Chart">UK R&amp;B Chart</a> on November 27, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKR.26BDebut_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKR.26BDebut-67">[67]</a></sup> It also debuted on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> at number 121 in the chart issue December 3, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uksingleschart-31211_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-uksingleschart-31211-68">[68]</a></sup> In the United States, the song debuted on the US <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100_Singles" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles">Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles</a> chart at number 17 in the chart issue December 10, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USBubbling_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-USBubbling-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other than "Talk That Talk", each single charted on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 Year-End issue. Furthermore, with "We Found Love" ending at No. 8 on the 2012 year-end tally, it marked the first time since 2007 that Rihanna ended the year with a top 10 song as lead artist.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"We Found Love" was the first performed song from the album, as it was performed for the first time on November 14, 2011 at Rihanna's <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a> (2011) in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-first-70">[70]</a></sup> On November 17, 2011 Rihanna performed the song on <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._season_1)" title="The X Factor (U.S. season 1)">first season</a> of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S.)" title="The X Factor (U.S.)">The X Factor USA</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-X_Factor_USA_performance_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-X_Factor_USA_performance-71">[71]</a></sup> On November 20, 2011 Rihanna performed the song on <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_8)" title="The X Factor (UK series 8)">eighth season</a> of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_UK" title="The X Factor UK">The X Factor UK</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-X_Factor_UK_performance_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-X_Factor_UK_performance-72">[72]</a></sup> On February 12, 2012, Rihanna performed "We Found Love" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Grammy_Awards" title="2012 Grammy Awards">2012 Grammy Awards</a> held at the <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grammys_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grammys-73">[73]</a></sup> followed by her duet single "<a href="/wiki/Princess_of_China" title="Princess of China">Princess of China</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> for first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grammys_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grammys-73">[73]</a></sup> Later that month, the singer performed the song at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_BRIT_Awards" title="2012 BRIT Awards">2012 BRIT Awards</a> held on February 21, 2012 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)" title="The O2 Arena (London)">The O2 Arena</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRITS_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRITS-74">[74]</a></sup> Whilst promoting her first feature film appearance in "<a href="/wiki/Battleship_(film)" title="Battleship (film)">Battleship</a>", Rihanna made a rare visit to <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, performing "We Found Love" on the Japanese music television program <a href="/wiki/Music_Station" title="Music Station">Music Station</a>. She donned a traditional <a href="/wiki/Kimono" title="Kimono">kimono</a> and concluded the performance by <a href="/wiki/Crowd_surfing" title="Crowd surfing">crowd surfing</a> into the audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1070" data-file-width="1600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg/220px-Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg/330px-Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg/440px-Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_live_at_Kollen_Music_Festival_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rihanna performing during <i>Kollen Music Festival</i> in June 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rihanna's first performance of "Talk That Talk" was made on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jonathan_Ross_Show" title="The Jonathan Ross Show">The Jonathan Ross Show</a></i>, in the United Kingdom, aired on March 3, 2012. The singer performed a solo version of the track, and was also interviewed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jonathan_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jonathan-76">[76]</a></sup> Rihanna performed "Where Have You Been" for the first time live at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Grammy Awards">2012 Post-Grammy Charity Fundraiser</a>, along with "We Found Love", on February 13, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On April 15, 2012, Rihanna performed the Song at the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a>, along with "We Found Love". She wasn't an official performer at the festival but she joined <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a> on his set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On May 5, 2012, Rihanna performed "Where Have You Been" and a Medley of "Birthday Cake" and "Talk That Talk" on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2012_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2012-79">[79]</a></sup> The performance of "Where Have You Been" featured an aesthetic similar to that of the music video; the <i>SNL</i> set was decorated in an <i><a href="/wiki/One_Thousand_and_One_Nights" title="One Thousand and One Nights">One Thousand and One Nights</a></i> fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2012_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2012-79">[79]</a></sup> Rihanna and her backup dancers performed a highly choreographed dance routine, the same as the music video, and they wore Arabian inspired outfits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2012_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2012-79">[79]</a></sup> The performance of the medley with the original interlude version of "Birthday Cake" and "Talk That Talk" started with the singer performing "Birthday Cake" and featured Rihanna in an all black outfit with a giant spiders web as the backdrop behind her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2012_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2012-79">[79]</a></sup> After she performed a short section of the song, it transitioned into "Talk That Talk", where she performed her part of the song in full, without the rap vocal by Jay-Z.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2012_79-4"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2012-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Documentary">Documentary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Documentary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Road to <i>Talk That Talk</i>" shows Rihanna behind the scenes during the production of the album. The first part of "Road to <i>Talk That Talk</i>" was released onto the internet on February 17, 2012. In the viral video Rihanna takes the cameras back stage on the last day of the <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a>, to the studio whilst she talks about the track listing and to <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> with her family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The second part of "Road to <i>Talk That Talk</i>" was released May 9, 2012 in which Rihanna videoed the rest of her trip to Barbados, to the hotel where she was with <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>, behind the photo shoots and she spoke on her breakdown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>

<p><b>Notes</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Track listing and credits from album booklet.</li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span></sup> signifies a vocal <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^b</a></b></span></sup> signifies a co-<a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
</ul>
<p><b>Sample credits</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_notes_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Album_notes-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"Where Have You Been" contains elements from the composition "<a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Been_Everywhere" title="I've Been Everywhere">I've Been Everywhere</a>" written by <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Mack" title="Geoff Mack">Geoff Mack</a>.</li>
<li>"Talk That Talk" contains samples from <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a> recording "I Got a Story to Tell" written by Anthony Best, Sean Combs, Carl Thompson and Christopher Wallace.</li>
<li>"Cockiness (Love It)" contains samples from Greg Kinnear's performance of "Summertime" in the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/Stuck_on_You_(film)" title="Stuck on You (film)">Stuck On You</a></i>, originally performed by <a href="/wiki/Billy_Stewart" title="Billy Stewart">Billy Stewart</a>, written by <a href="/wiki/DuBose_Heyward" title="DuBose Heyward">DuBose Heyward</a>.</li>
<li>"Drunk on Love" contains samples from the recording "Intro" as performed by <a href="/wiki/The_xx" title="The xx">The xx</a> and written by Baria Qureshi, Romy Madley Croft, Oliver Sim and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_xx" title="Jamie xx">Jamie Smith</a>.</li>
<li>"Red Lipstick" contains interpolations from the composition "<a href="/wiki/Wherever_I_May_Roam" title="Wherever I May Roam">Wherever I May Roam</a>" as performed by <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> and written by <a href="/wiki/James_Hetfield" title="James Hetfield">James Hetfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lars_Ulrich" title="Lars Ulrich">Lars Ulrich</a>. Contains a sample from the sound recording "Saxon" performed by <a href="/wiki/Chase_%26_Status" title="Chase &amp; Status">Chase &amp; Status</a> and written by William Kennard and Saul Milton.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_formats">Release formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Talk_That_Talk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i><b>Talk That Talk</b></i> (Standard edition)</p>
<ul>
<li>Standard 11 tracks, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewel_case" title="Jewel case">jewel case</a> packaging</li>
</ul>
<p><i><b>Talk That Talk (Deluxe edition)</b></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Standard 11 tracks along with 3 bonus tracks</li>
<li>16-page photobook</li>
<li>Folded mini poster</li>
<li>Two photo cards</li>
<li>Perfume sample special card (for US deluxe packages only)</li>
<li>Package <a href="/wiki/Digipak" title="Digipak">8-panel digipak</a></li>
</ul>
<p><b><i>Talk That Talk</i> (iTunes edition)</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Standard 11 tracks along with 3 bonus tracks</li>
<li>We Found Love (Calvin Harris extended mix)</li>
<li>Digital booklet</li>
</ul>
